Soviet Russia Protests to Japan Over the China Eastern Railway Issue 48

Japanese Puppets Deliberately Provoke Russia, Creating a Serious Situation

Demanding Effective Measures to Protect Soviet Russian Interests

(Moscow) Regarding the tense situation on the China Eastern Railway, Soviet Deputy Commissar for Foreign Affairs Karakhan lodged a protest with Japanese Ambassador Ota on April 16. This news has been officially released by TASS and published in today's newspapers. It is reported that Karakhan invited Ota to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs on that day and made the following remarks on behalf of the Soviet government:

Deliberately Provoking Conflicts: "Since the outbreak of the Sino-Japanese conflict and the entry of Japanese troops into Manchuria, the Japanese government has repeatedly expressed through its ambassador in Moscow and directly to the Soviet ambassador in Japan, guarantees not to infringe upon Soviet interests, especially regarding the China Eastern Railway. The Soviet government accepted these guarantees with considerable trust, especially in the beginning, as the Manchurian local authorities seemed quite willing to avoid any actions that would discriminate against Soviet interests. Therefore, when the China Eastern Railway suffered serious damage, the Soviet government drew the attention of Japan without feeling particularly anxious, explaining everything as the impact of the military situation. However, in recent months, the actions of the 'puppet state' authorities and their Japanese advisors, as well as the Japanese officials in Manchuria, have directly created a serious situation on the China Eastern Railway, causing alarm to the Soviet government. This is not only due to the state into which the railway has fallen, but also because of the deliberate provocation of conflicts on various issues, making the entire situation increasingly serious. The Soviet government wishes to draw the Japanese government's attention to the following fundamental facts:

Illegally Occupying Wharves: On July 7, 1932, the 'puppet state' authorities seized the China Eastern Railway wharf in Harbin. The Soviet government notified the Japanese government the next day that this action was directly guided by Japanese employed by the 'puppet state.' This matter damaged the interests of the China Eastern Railway but has not yet been resolved. On April 11 of this year, Japanese troops occupied the wharf office, raised the Japanese flag, and posted Japanese guards. Even if the previous illegal actions were committed by the 'puppet state,' the Japanese authorities have now occupied the wharf that is still under negotiation. The Soviet Union cannot but protest this action. Owing Huge Amounts of Freight Fees: The Soviet government agreed to the Japanese government's request to transport Japanese troops on the China Eastern Railway. It was agreed in advance to pay freight fees on time, so it was considered a purely commercial matter. However, negotiations between the China Eastern Railway and the Japanese authorities on the issue of payment were subjected to systematic delays. The accumulated debt has now reached a huge amount, increasing the railway's economic difficulties, as the railway's commercial transportation has been greatly affected by military operations in Manchuria.

Destroying Eurasian Transportation: What shocked the Soviet government most about the recent situation in Manchuria was the series of coercive actions taken by the police authorities under the direct orders and participation of Japanese officials on the Manchurian side to disrupt the normal operation of the China Eastern Railway and cause serious losses to Soviet interests. This included cutting off the tracks connecting the China Eastern Railway to the Outer Baikal Railway, damaging the Soviet Union's right to access the China Eastern Railway by train, obstructing Eurasian transportation, and seizing goods transported by the Soviet Union, etc. The eastern section of the China Eastern Railway is now in a completely disorganized state due to systematic attacks on vehicles and assassinations and kidnappings of Soviet people employed by the railway. The Japanese government guaranteed that it would transport troops on the railway to restore order, but in reality, the order and security of the railway are now worse than before. Detention of Cars Without Error: Regarding the disputed issue of locomotives and cars, Karakhan declared that the Soviet government was in no error in this matter. The locomotives were the property of the Soviet Union and never belonged to the China Eastern Railway from the beginning. As for the cars, there are currently 2,000 of Soviet cars on the China Eastern Railway, exceeding the number of China Eastern Railway cars in the Soviet Union. The delay in their exchange and return is due to the military conflict between the Chinese troops and the Japanese-Manchurian troops.

Russians Subjected to Abuse: Karakhan then protested against the large-scale arrests of Soviet people, saying, "Most of them have been detained for more than a year without trial and have been subjected to extraordinary abuse by the Japanese gendarmerie and the Japanese employed by 'Manchukuo.' Of course, these facts are not the entirety of the facts infringing on Soviet interests, but the Soviet government has had to remind the Japanese government of the guarantees it made earlier and demand effective measures to earnestly protect Soviet interests."

Demanding a Prompt Reply: In conclusion, Karakhan requested the Japanese ambassador to provide a prompt reply. Ota promised to immediately convey Karakhan's views to the Japanese government. At the same time, Karakhan handed Ota a memorandum regarding the recent disputed issue of locomotives and cars. (TASS Dispatch, Eighteenth Day)

Japan Plans to Ignore It: (Tokyo) The Japanese Foreign Ministry has not yet received the lengthy note verbale submitted by the Soviet Russian government authorities to the Japanese ambassador to Russia regarding the China Eastern Railway incident and does not know its contents. If it is a protest to Japan regarding the China Eastern Railway issue, Japan, considering the issue to be one between the "puppet state" and Russia and unrelated to Japan, plans to dismiss the protest without consideration. If it is a request for Japan to mediate, then it may consider appropriate measures. (Jiji Dispatch, Eighteenth Day)

Denying Manipulation of White Russians: (Tokyo) The Soviet ambassador to Japan visited Foreign Minister Uchida at the Japanese Foreign Ministry today to negotiate the dispute over the China Eastern Railway. It is reported that the Soviet ambassador expressed dissatisfaction with the Japanese government's repeated instigation of puppet organizations to provoke Russia. The Soviet Union deeply hopes to resolve the dispute peacefully and stated that Japan should immediately cease manipulating the anti-Soviet activities of the White Russians, otherwise it would be cause for concern in the diplomatic relations between the two countries. Foreign Minister Uchida replied that the Japanese side also hopes to resolve the China Eastern Railway issue peacefully, but the matter concerns the "puppet state" and Japan cannot act alone. As for the use of White Russians, it is not the case. The Japanese Foreign Ministry, based on Far Eastern peace, is willing to continue negotiations with the Soviet Union. (Hualian Dispatch, Eighteenth Day)

The Puppet State Takes Advantage of Power: (Harbin) The Soviet side claims ownership of the locomotive, but this locomotive, although ordered from the United States during the Kerensky government era, was not delivered to Soviet Russia when the Russian Revolution broke out. The United States delivered it to the anti-Soviet side, and the factory equipment and installation costs were all paid by the China Eastern Railway. Therefore, it is actually owned by the China Eastern Railway. Now, the Soviet side has opened it into Russian territory without any notification, which is clearly infringing on the sovereignty of the "puppet state." The "puppet state" is preparing to thoroughly condemn it and expresses a strong determination. Negotiations will not be accepted under any circumstances until the damage is resolved. (Dentsu Dispatch)

(Changchun) Regarding the Soviet Russian government's protest on the Eastern Railway issue, the (puppet) Ministry of Communications will issue a rebuttal reply, pointing out that it is unreasonable, and will lodge a serious protest against the Soviet side's arbitrary removal of freight cars and similar illegal acts. The protest letter will be delivered to Koznetov by Li Shaogeng, the Director of the Eastern Railway, today. (Dentsu Dispatch, Eighteenth Day)

Japan Covets the China Eastern Railway: (Tokyo) The Nichi Nichi Shimbun reports that, according to reliable sources, it received a telegram from Harbin today stating that Soviet Russia is now preparing to sell its interests in the China Eastern Railway to Japan for 100 million yuan. It is reported that a certain important person is currently in Harbin negotiating the sale of Soviet Russian interests with the "Manchukuo" authorities. Today, the spokesman of the Ministry of the Army denied that this was the case and made a half-humorous statement, saying, "If this statement is indeed true, 'Manchukuo' will also be unable to purchase this. If Soviet Russia wants to sell its interests, it must lower the selling price." (Reuters Dispatch, Eighteenth Day)

Russia-Japan Fishing Issue 49

The Situation is Extremely Dangerous

The Tokyo Jiji Shinpo reported on the 14th that, according to information obtained by the Hakodate Maritime Police Department, the Soviet Russian government is repeatedly blocking the fish passages of Russian state-owned fishing grounds by deploying nets by Japanese fishing boats outside the three nautical miles off the coast of Kamchatka, causing serious damage to Russian fishermen. Since this year, areas within twelve nautical miles from various locations in our country have been recognized as Russian territorial waters, and Japanese fishing boats will be expelled. This project was approved by the Far Eastern Executive Committee and notified to the Japanese government. That is, the Russian domestic law will be implemented, but the Japanese government authorities believe that areas outside three nautical miles from the coast belong to the high seas and reject this notice. The Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry has instructed 400 fishing boats carrying 7,000 fishermen to continue fishing in the Sea of Kamchatka. If Russia insists on the twelve-nautical-mile claim and expels Japanese fishing boats, it will use force to deal with them. It is reported that Russia has dispatched armed surveillance ships such as the Alostny to patrol the Sea of Kamchatka. Therefore, Japanese fishing boats are also equipped with machine guns and rifles, preparing to fight the surveillance ships. On the 12th, Pacific Fisheries Commissioner Miura and others reported to the Hakodate Maritime Police Department that they were about to use force, and the situation was extremely dangerous.

Over 200,000 White Russians in the Four Eastern Provinces 50

Organized by Japanese Special Service Department

Resettled Along the China Eastern Railway

(Tokyo) After the September 18th Incident, Japanese special service agencies specifically studied manipulating White Russians to resist the Soviet Union. White Russian leader Semyonov had close relations with the Kwantung Army Special Service Department. The number of White Russians wandering around the world who have flowed into the three eastern provinces has reached 200,000, of whom former soldiers of the Russian Empire make up the majority. After several contacts with White Russian leaders, the Japanese Special Service Department decided to organize former soldiers of the Russian Empire and young White Russians into immigrant groups, give them strict military training, and scatter them in several groups to key military locations along the China Eastern Railway. In peacetime, they will support themselves by farming, and in wartime, they will be used as vanguards for invading Russia. Women, children, and the elderly are allowed to engage in commerce in the cities. Recently, taking advantage of the disputes over the China Eastern Railway issue, they plan to use force to expel Soviet personnel and replace them with White Russian personnel. (Eighteenth Day Special Dispatch)

US Secretary of War Advocates Great Naval Policy 51

Maintaining the Monroe Doctrine

Existing Strength More Than Sufficient

Promoting Far Eastern Policy

Great Navy Necessary for Success

(Tokyo) The Japanese Ambassador to the United States, Debuchi, telegraphed the Japanese Foreign Ministry yesterday from the United States, stating that the US Secretary of War has consistently advocated a policy of self-reliance and recently published an article in a naval magazine entitled "Never Forget." The article advocated expanding the US Navy and abandoning the previous cautious approach. The sudden change in the attitude of US naval figures has caused great consternation in the Japanese Foreign Ministry, which has reportedly reported to the cabinet to prepare countermeasures (Associated Press Dispatch, Eighteenth Day) Washington-The current naval policy of the United States government is to actively expand to the holding levels permitted by the London Treaty. The basis of its advocacy is that the naval powers of the world are currently divided into three pillars: the United Kingdom, the United States, and Japan. To seek a balance of power and maintain peace, all parties must not lack the treaty tonnage of naval power. If the purpose of the United States is only to implement the Caribbean policy (surrounding the Caribbean Sea southeast of the Gulf of Mexico and using military force to interfere in the internal affairs of countries such as Nicaragua, Panama, and Cuba) and maintain the Monroe Doctrine, then its existing naval power is already sufficient. If it needs to further promote the Far Eastern policy, then the implementation of a great naval policy is necessary for success. The naval power of the United States is now behind Japan, so Japan dares to run rampant in Manchuria. From the perspective of implementing national policy, the existence or absence of a great navy is the key to the success or failure of the Far Eastern policy. Rear Admiral Black, Director of the Bureau of Ships, forcefully stated that in order to maintain overseas trade and the dignity of a first-class country, the United States absolutely needs to maintain the world's top naval power. The extent of the US naval expansion must be based on: 1. The protection of overseas trade; 2. The defense of scattered American colonies overseas; 3. The key to maintaining the implementation of national policy; 4. Obtaining a balanced peace based on the treaty tonnage of the three major naval powers; 5. Guaranteeing victory in future naval battles. The so-called war here is undoubtedly targeting Japan. (World News Agency)

US Arms Embargo Against Aggressor Nations 84

House of Representatives Passes Granting Special Powers to the President

Severe Penalties for Violating the Law

Reuters, Washington, 17th - Today, the House of Representatives passed a bill granting the President the power to prohibit the export of arms to aggressor nations. Anyone who violates this law will be subject to a fine of US$10,000 or imprisonment for two years.

National News Agency, Washington, 17th - When the US arms embargo bill was passed in the House of Representatives today by a vote of 252 to 110, many members strongly stated that the passage of this bill was tantamount to coercing Japan, but the bill was eventually passed. The bill has now been sent to the Senate. Administrative members have requested the Senate to vote on it as soon as possible. The administrative members also explained to the Senate that the United States is the only country in the world whose administrative organs lack the power to embargo. The current US action is directly based on the UK's temporary ban on arms exports to China and Japan. When the UK lifted the ban, the British Ambassador to the US, Lindsay, visited the US State Department to inquire about the US's attitude towards this matter. Perhaps Lindsay at that time expressed to the US authorities his support for the embargo. Whether this is true or not, the US government's arms embargo bill was submitted to Congress the day after Lindsay's visit to the State Department. Furthermore, there was a similar proposal from the cabinet side during the Hoover era, but the scope required by Hoover at that time was extremely narrow, limited only to the Latin American countries of South America. The powers now requested by Roosevelt are broader and not limited to the Western Hemisphere. In the future, the United States will unite with the United Kingdom, and all countries at war or about to be at war will be subject to the same embargo treatment. During the House debate today, Representative Tinkham declared that the passage of this bill would harm Japan's feelings. He, as the leader of the Republican opposition, expressed his opposition and wanted to amend several clauses of the original bill in order to maintain the neutrality of the United States. These amendments, if passed, would greatly restrict the President's powers, but they were all rejected one by one.

Senate Rejects Silver Coin Minting Bill 85

Reuters, New York, 18th - According to a New York Times dispatch from Washington, the Senate rejected a bill to mint silver coins at a ratio of sixteen to one with gold coins, because President Roosevelt must negotiate an international agreement on the bimetallic standard with the five countries of Britain, France, Germany, Italy, and Japan. The purpose of this agreement is to have a stable exchange rate between the currencies of various countries, so as to avoid the constant fluctuations in international exchange rates. Secretary of State Hull has discussed with British Ambassador Lindsay the methods to accomplish this. If a multilateral treaty can be concluded, it will be sufficient to encourage international purchases of silver.

Lawyers Defend Wick's Case, British Technicians Will Receive Lighter Sentences 86

Anglo-Russian Diplomatic Relations Expected to Ease

Reuters, Moscow, 17th - The lawyers for the Russian defendants, Guzev, Sokolov, and Valeni, Kashnatsiev, strongly defended their clients during the continued hearing of the Wick Company technicians case tonight, hoping to shift all the responsibility to the British technicians, saying that before the court judges this case, please do not forget that Guzev was not an active counter-revolutionary before meeting MacDonald and Thornton, and that MacDonald and Sangdon denied their confessions, saying that they signed them under pressure, while Guzev and others admitted it without hesitation, so their crimes should be reduced. Furthermore, Sokolov is only a second-class saboteur, and a ten-year prison sentence is sufficient. As for Valeni, it is hoped that the court will give him a chance to reform himself and serve Soviet Russia. The Russian lawyer Shi Huazi, representing the Russian defendants Solin, Klasningov, and Sokolujin, argued in court that Sokolujin's crime was indeed serious, but he was surrounded by anti-Russian and saboteurs, and his circumstances were excusable. Klasningov himself confessed his guilt and expressed remorse, asking the court to spare his life. The lawyer's words were not touching and were not noticed by the court. Observers coughed deliberately to stop him, and even laughed wildly. Pinas, who defended Shebert and others, accused Nordhua of inducing his client to engage in espionage and falling into crime, asking the court to consider the youth of his client and give him leniency. Smirnov, MacDonald's lawyer, spoke movingly, saying that MacDonald came from a humble background and was disabled. He came to Russia to serve, but he did not know the prohibitions of the country. He happened to meet the insidious Guzev, who was a villain and would sell his country for a few hundred rubles. MacDonald worked for the Wick Company and had been trained since childhood to maintain the company's honor and interests. The company instructed him to collect information, so he did so as instructed. MacDonald was a subordinate. It would be unfair to punish him in the same way as the superiors, Monkhouse and Thornton. MacDonald did commit a serious crime, but he solemnly declared that he would not do it again. In the future, MacDonald can serve Soviet Russia. The court adjourned at 10:15 tonight and will resume the hearing at 10:00 AM on the 18th. Reuters reporters learned that the defendants may be punished as follows: MacDonald and Thornton, each with a ten-year prison sentence; Monkhouse, a three-year prison sentence; Keshni and Nordhua released on bail; Gregory acquitted. The Russian defendants, Guzev and Lovanov, may be sentenced to death, while other Russians will be sentenced to imprisonment. It is expected that the British defendants' sentences can be reduced to exile, because Prosecutor Vyshinsky said that Russia does not want bloodshed and revenge. The British here have a lot of comforting criticism of the prosecutor's moderate claims and the UK's actions regarding trade with Russia, and it is expected that a moderate verdict will be an important element in the future diplomatic relations between Britain and Russia.

Last Trial Situation The case against six British and twelve Russian people of Wick Company opened the final day of trial today. There were many onlookers in the court because it was expected that the lawyers of the British defendants, Brown and others, would have a debate. Brown said: The client Thornton has withdrawn his testimony to the political detective bureau, and now I will explain everything so that the judges understand that Thornton is actually innocent. It is now pointed out that Thornton induced sabotage, who had already been engaged in sabotage work before meeting Thornton. They are traitors to Russia and gave news to Thornton in exchange for money. Thornton expected that the Soviet Union would compete with Britain, so he wanted to get economic news. What he unwittingly funded to obtain was economic news rather than espionage. Bribery is more common in Britain than in Russia, Brown said after speaking for 45 minutes, Nordhua's lawyer Damashevsky continued to speak, saying that Nordhua did not have much contact with Lobanov and his sabotage party, and MacDonald and others did not prove that Nordhua was a saboteur, so he asked the court to release Nordhua, the hope of liberation after the application by his lawyer, Gregory's release is really promising, so his lawyer did not say much, Keshni's lawyer Lidoff denied each of the accusations, saying that the documentary evidence was insufficient, Mr. K. was confident in himself, and had long denied everything."

After that, there was a surprising statement. When Comodoreff spoke to defend Wick's manager, Monkhouse, he said that Mr. Meng was charged with three things: espionage, slacking, and bribery, but Mr. Meng only denied bribery. Mr. Meng was guilty, and it was difficult for me to defend him. I don't want to shift the crime to others, Mr. Meng and Thornton have been in Russia for many years and have a close relationship with each other, but according to the evidence, Thornton has never informed Mr. Meng of his activities, after the lawyers spoke, the defendants successively陈诉供词, repeatedly changed his confession, and this time also admitted his guilt, saying, "I am guilty, what else can I say, Nordhua then said, I am innocent, and I have always been a friend of the Soviet Union, Keshni also said, I am innocent, no matter what the sentence is, I will always be an honest person, Monkhouse said, Some people say that I cheated the British government about the 18-hour questioning, but in fact this statement is not true, I was misunderstood, and I do not admit guilt to all three points, said Sangdon, I stated that I was not guilty at the beginning of the trial, and I still am like that," All the Russian defendants then confessed their guilt, The court adjourned at 3:30 p.m. to consider the verdict, (Reuters, Moscow, 18th)

Japanese Invent Anti-Aircraft Weapon 87

Japan Alliance News Tokyo Correspondence A reservist living in Kumamoto Prefecture, in view of the seriousness of the situation, invented a new type of weapon called "Light Anti-Aircraft Gun." The inventor is named Yoshi Katsuki, 39 years old, and joined the 56th Infantry Regiment in Taisho 4 (1915), promoted to lance corporal, and after two years of painstaking research, he was able to invent this new type of weapon. The "Light Anti-Aircraft Gun" has six gun barrels, and for objects moving at high speeds, such as aircraft, it automatically determines the standard and can fire freely, and its structure is quite sophisticated.

At a time when the World Economic Conference and its preliminary discussions are seeking to eliminate international commercial barriers, India has canceled the trade agreement with Japan and implemented anti-dumping measures, which is a sigh for the future of international trade. The Future of the Japanese Government 90

Saito's Attitude Turns Active

Holding a Resolve to Dissolve Parliament

Dentsu, Tokyo, 18th - Prime Minister Saito's instructions at the local governors' meeting showed no intention of resigning, giving a great impulse to all parties. Although the surface seems calm, most of them are surprised and think it is necessary to change the future countermeasures. Generally speaking, Prime Minister Saito regards the purification of the political world as an important mission, and may inevitably dissolve the parliament. Even if Finance Minister Takahashi resigns, he will supplement it and reorganize the cabinet. At this time, if the Seiyukai cabinet members generally retreat, they will also be supplemented. If the Seiyukai holds an opposing attitude in the next regular parliamentary session, the parliament will be dissolved. It is said that Prime Minister Saito has indeed made this decision, but it is doubtful whether the surrounding situation will allow the Prime Minister's decision. From the Prime Minister's instructions at the local governors' meeting, it can be seen that the political situation will become more complicated again.

News from the Border Regions Regarding Military Liaison 92

Tang Yulin's troops are west of Fengning.

Sun Zhanying's troops are in the vicinity of Chicheng.

(Beiping dispatch) Since the fall of Rehe, various armies have concentrated in the vicinity of the Chahar-Rehe border, actively replenishing their forces in preparation for a counteroffensive. However, due to the blocked transportation and lack of news from the area, Mr. Wu Lei-yuan, the commander-in-chief of the 5th Route of the National Anti-Japanese Army in Rehe, returned to Beiping yesterday from western Fengning. His account of the situation is quite practical and is recorded below for the reference of those who are interested:

Mr. Wu said, "During the recent westward invasion by the Japanese, the First Division of our army, led by Liu Pin, engaged in combat with the enemy in Chaoyang, suffering heavy losses after several hand-to-hand battles. Later, due to changes in strategy, the National Army withdrew, and all the cavalry of that division also retreated westward, providing cover. Currently, the brigade of Tan Pingfang from that division has reached the area of Aobao Temple, northeast of Dolun, where they are confronting the enemy. There are occasional small skirmishes at the outposts. As for the Second Division of our army, led by Xu Xiyao, they were originally in Chifeng. After the fall of Chifeng, they retreated westward with the 41st Army and are now stationed in the area of Sanyuhao, Sanzueshan, and Qipanshan, east of Dolun. I personally led the various units of the Third Division and arrived in the area of Wudaoying, west of Fengning, on March 26th. At that time, the commander of the 41st Army, Sun, was stationed in Dagetown, so I personally went to discuss the concentration point of our army and seek liaison. I was warmly welcomed and generously assisted by Commander Sun. I also met with Feng Yangtian, the Chief of Staff, who issued a notice to all units to adopt unified action. At the same time, it was decided to station troops in the Lama Mountain, Xishuigou, Ganshuigou, and Datan areas. Unexpectedly, the situation at the front changed a few days ago, and Fengning fell on March 28th. At that time, our army engaged with the enemy at the Toutaoyingzi north of Fengning, fighting fiercely for two hours. Due to being outnumbered, we suffered more than twenty casualties. At this time, Commander Sun moved westward from Dagetown. On the morning of the 29th, two Japanese planes bombed Dagetown, destroying several civilian houses and injuring two villagers. On the afternoon of the same day, I led my troops to move westward in coordination with the main force. We are now concentrated in the Pingdingshan, Yunwugou, and Lamagou areas, strictly defending. West of Fengning, there are also troops of Tang Yulin. When a portion of our army arrived in Datan, we sent a liaison officer to contact Cui, the Chief of Staff of Tang, and Tang, the section chief. Cui and Tang said that they represented Chairman Tang and were willing to do their utmost to assist and to notify all armies to take coordinated action. Currently, Chicheng, Zhanyuan, and Yanqing are all garrisoned by the 41st Army. Commander Sun himself has now arrived in Chicheng. At present, a large army is gathering at the front, and all units have established liaison and set up defensive works. However, there is a severe lack of supplies and clothing. I have come to Beiping specifically to handle rear supply and military affairs, and I urgently need to seek instructions from Chairman He, so I will return to the front soon," he said. (16th)

He Jian Arrives in Jiangxi to Meet Chiang Kai-shek 93

The Hunan Army Advances Towards Ji'an After Capturing Yongxin.

The Central Route Army in Eastern Jiangxi Recovers Yongfeng.

Zhu De and Mao Zedong Have a Tendency to Flee into Ningdu.

(Nanchang dispatch) The Hunan Army has entered Jiangxi to assist in suppressing bandits. Those who have arrived in western and northern Jiangxi, in addition to the original troops of Tao Guang, have recently been joined by the troops of Wang Dongyuan, Peng Weiren, Chen Guangzhong, and others. The 　　division in the Wanzai area has already contacted the Hubei Army and is jointly attacking the forces of Kong Hechong from three sides, having recovered Xiaoyuan. Those on the Jiangxi-Hunan border have already contacted the Guangdong Army and are jointly suppressing the forces of Li Tianzhu along with Wang Maode and others, having also recovered Ninggang and Lianhua. In order to concentrate the forces in Jiangxi to suppress Zhu De and Mao Zedong, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek has decided to transfer the responsibility for suppressing bandits in the border areas of Jiangxi to the neighboring provinces bordering Jiangxi. West of the Gan River is the responsibility of Hunan's He Jian, and he has been telegraphed to Jiangxi to give instructions. He arrived in Xun on the 14th and took a special train to Nanchang that night, arriving at 10 p.m. and staying at the Jiangxi Grand Hotel. According to He, "I came to Jiangxi this time upon receiving Chairman Chiang's telegram to ask for instructions on the plan to jointly suppress the communist bandits on the Jiangxi-Hunan border, and to report on the military and political situation in Hunan. The communists in Hunan have been largely suppressed. I am now supervising the troops to enter Jiangxi and engage in joint suppression. Liu Jianxu has already gone to Wanzai from Changsha to supervise the division," and so on. On the morning of the 15th, He went to the Science Museum to meet Chiang Kai-shek. Chiang hosted a reception for He that evening at his headquarters, with He Guoguang and others as companions, and they discussed the joint suppression plan for Hunan, Jiangxi, and Hubei. It did not end until late at night. He also visited Xiong Shihui, He Guoguang, and others to exchange views on bandit suppression. It is said that he is scheduled to return to Hunan today (16th) or tomorrow.

The Hunan Army's bandit suppression in Jiangxi has progressed quite rapidly recently. According to telegrams from Chen Guangzhong and Wang Dongyuan, they captured the only base of the bandits, Yongxin County, on the 13th, completely destroying more than ten institutions such as the headquarters of the false Jiangxi-Hunan Border Military Region, the false Eighth Army headquarters, the false Jiangxi Provincial Government, the Yongxin Soviet, and military hospitals. However, Yongxin has been occupied by bandits for six years, and the suffering of the people and the destruction are self-evident. Division Commander Chen has telegraphed the provincial government and Commissioner Li of the Tenth District to send people to deal with the aftermath. As for Li Tianzhu's bandits, they are actively fleeing towards the Yuan River and Gan River, with the loss of Yongxin, Ninggang, and Lianhua on the Jiangxi-Hunan border. The Hunan and Hubei armies are also pursuing and suppressing the bandits. The vanguard of the 　　division has reached Ji'an. It is said that Ji'an will also be handed over to the Hunan Army to be responsible for it, so that the troops originally stationed in Ji'an can be transferred to the east bank of the Gan River to besiege Zhu De and Mao Zedong. As for eastern Jiangxi, since the Central Route Army recovered Xingan, the false 135th Army Corps in the central section of the Gan River has retreated to the southeast. A certain division recovered Yongfeng County on the 15th. The false 21st and 2nd bandit armies retreated to the west of Chongren and Le'an, echoing the bandits south of Yihuang. A certain department led by me, advancing south from Yongfeng and Le'an, has already passed Zhukeng. The capture of Le'an County is imminent. Zhu De and Mao Zedong's false First Front Army have a tendency to flee into Ningdu. (April 16th)

Communist Banditry Re-ignites in Hubei Province 94

Xu Xiangqian's Troops Harass Macheng and Huang'an Counties

Fan Xiji Urges Sichuan and Hunan Armies to Jointly Suppress He Long

(Hankou dispatch) After suffering a defeat last year, the main force of the communist bandits in Hubei Province fled elsewhere, while sporadic bandits remained hidden in various places, attempting to revive. However, due to the strict defenses of the stationed troops and local militias, they were unable to succeed. This year, as the Japanese invaders have become more aggressive, the authorities have concentrated their efforts on defending against the invaders and saving the nation. As a result, there has been some troop movement in Hubei Province. He Long's remnant bandits were able to return to western Hubei, and Xu Xiangqian's remaining bandits in Hubei also took the opportunity to rise up in the northeast. Last month, Xu's bandits gathered scattered elements into an organized force, unearthed hidden weapons, and seized firearms from the stationed troops and local militias, totaling about 6,000 men. They were organized into the false 24th, 25th, and 28th armies, occupying the southwest of Lihuang County (formerly Jinjiazai), the northwest of Macheng County, and the area between Huang'an and Jingfu (formerly Xinxie) counties. They also moved back and forth in the area bordering the south of Shangcheng and the north of Macheng, concentrating their forces to launch fierce attacks on the stationed troops and local militias. As a result, the Qinkang area of Shangcheng, and the Dongyizhou and Futian River areas of Macheng were all ravaged. The National Army division stationed there was unable to gather at the same time due to the vastness of the area under its defense, nor could it maintain a line of defense at every point, allowing the bandits to operate. On the 17th, according to a telephone report from Song's troops, the bridges along the Han'an highway were destroyed by the bandits, and traffic was suddenly cut off. The severity of the situation can be imagined. Currently, the 　　and other units are separately suppressing the bandits. The local militias of Jingfu, Lihuang, Huang'an, and Macheng counties have also been organized by Zheng, the county magistrate of Macheng, to implement joint defense, and have requested the headquarters to issue ammunition to facilitate joint suppression.

In western Hubei, He's bandits still occupy Wuling Pass, and Fan Xiji is still in Enshi. Although there are widespread rumors of a three-pronged general offensive against the bandits, there are no confirmed reports of contact. Based on speculation, it may still be in the planning stage. There are several reasons why Fan's troops are slow to launch an offensive: first, the mountainous roads are rugged and inconvenient for troop movement; second, the roads are remote, and food supplies are insufficient; and third, friendly armies from Hunan and Sichuan have been slow to arrive and have failed to establish liaison. Chen Quzhen's troops of the Hunan Army have been searching for scattered bandits near the Hunan border and have not yet moved towards Hubei. Although one regiment of Wang Lingji's troops of the Sichuan Army has been mobilized, they have not dared to advance deeply due to their limited strength. On the 14th, Fan convened a military and political meeting in Shi, attended by the county magistrates of Enshi, Hefeng, Badong, Xianfeng, Lichuan, Jianshi, and Laifeng, as well as officers above the rank of regimental commander of the stationed troops. It concluded on the 16th. It is said that the meeting discussed the reform of general administration in each county and the progress of bandit suppression. At the same time, it abolished exorbitant taxes and prohibited the troops from harassing the people. It is said that Fan has been ordered by Chiang to also be responsible for rectifying general administration. However, the stalemate between the troops and the bandits is ultimately not a good policy. Fan has now telegraphed the Sichuan and Hunan armies, urging them to set out as soon as possible and agree on a joint suppression to achieve the effect of encirclement. (April 17th)

Suzhou Money Houses Discuss Abolishing Taels and Adopting the Yuan 97

Yesterday (18th) afternoon at 1:00 p.m., various money houses in Suzhou held a meeting at the Money Industry Association to discuss business strategies after the abolition of taels and the adoption of the yuan. As a result, it was decided that Suzhou would serve as a modern silver dollar port. In the future, all transactions would be based on modern silver dollars, and premiums would be abolished, and the operations would be the same as banks. The effective date was set for May 1st. As for the detailed business rules, due to time constraints, it was decided to reconvene at a later date.

Minister of Finance T.V. Soong, representing China at the Washington Economic Conference, set sail for the United States yesterday afternoon aboard the Dollar Line's President Jackson. It is expected that the ship will arrive in Seattle in early May and then proceed to Washington. No fewer than three to four hundred people from military, political, commercial, industrial, Chinese, and Western circles in the city, as well as relatives and friends of the Soong family, went to the pier to see him off. Soong also issued a written statement to the press on board. The details are recorded below:

(Photo by Xu Tianzhang: T.V. Soong and those seeing him off)

Yesterday morning, the Customs Wharf and the police specially dispatched Chinese and Western detectives to provide security in the vicinity. Wen Hongen, the director of the Public Security Bureau, personally led armed police officers to maintain order at the wharf. All irrelevant people were not allowed to enter. The security was exceptionally tight. However, those who came to see off were allowed to participate without a pass. Therefore, despite the light rain and the chilly spring air, those seeing off arrived one after another, with great enthusiasm.

Those Seeing Him Off

Tang Hai'an, the superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, arrived earliest. Others included the French Consul General in Shanghai, Meriel; the commander of the U.S. Marine Corps, Kyle Gao; Minister of Transportation Zhu Jiahua and his wife; Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs Liu Chongjie; Vice Minister of Finance Zou Lin; Mayor Wu Tiecheng; Director of Security Yang Hu; Government Advisor Sir Robert Hotung; Senior Advisor to the Ministry of Finance Zhang Shouyong; Secretary of the Ministry of Finance Zhou Xiangxian; Yang Dezhao, representative of Chen Jitang; Xiao Zhenying, representative of Song Zheyuan; Liu Yunfang, representative of Wang Zhengting; General Customs Commissioner Frederick Maze; Director of the Mint Lu Xuepu; General Zhu Qinglan, member of the Flood Relief Committee; Xi Dejiong and Zhou Bangjun of the National Economic Council; Guo Dehua, Secretary of the Ministry of Finance; He Shaofen, staff member of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs; Wen Yingxing, commander of the Revenue Police Corps; Li Fuxun and Xu Xinliu, representatives of the banking community; Wen Lant亭, representative of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce; Yang Jie, president of the Army University; Liu Hongsheng, Tang Shoumin, Du Yuesheng, Yu Qiaqing, and other business leaders; as well as Mrs. Zhang Leyi, T.V. Soong's wife, and his children Liangzi and An, totaling three to four hundred people.

Ferries and Flower Baskets

Soong and his family were on the Jinghui launch. The cabin was filled with about a hundred flower baskets presented by various sectors. Boarding Situation

At 10:45 a.m., Soong, accompanied by his wife Zhang Leyi and their son, arrived at the Customs Wharf by car. Sir Robert Hotung also arrived at this time. Soong shook hands with each of those seeing him off, repeatedly saying goodbye, and his attitude was exceptionally humble. At the same time, the Mingxing Company and Paramount Company competed to film Soong. Then, Tang Hai'an led Soong and others to board the Jinghui launch. A portion of those seeing him off also boarded other ferries to accompany him. They docked alongside the President Jackson at Bailianjing at 11:15 a.m., and then boarded the ship one after another. At that time, it was exactly 11:15 a.m. His acquaintances warmly greeted him and congratulated him on the success of his trip. Soong expressed his pleasure in accepting it. It was not until 11:50 a.m. that those seeing him off left the ship and returned. The President Jackson set sail at noon at 12:00 p.m. Those who traveled with Soong included Pei Songsun, president of the Bank of China; Young, advisor to the Ministry of Finance; Qin Yingchun, counselor of the Ministry of Finance; as well as secretaries Huang Chundao and Cai Shousheng; Wei Wenbin, secretary of the Chinese Embassy in the United States; and attendants Zhang Rong and Huang Zhenlin.　　Delivered a Speech

At the time of departure, Soong delivered a written speech on board, saying that the majority of the issues to be discussed at the World Economic Conference are related to the relations between countries, but also have a variety of significant relationships with China. Therefore, Ambassador Shi to the United States first sent a telegram to him, inviting him to attend. Later, Ambassadors Yan and Gu also sent telegrams, hoping that he would attend. At the same time, the government also decided to appoint him to go because the economic situation worldwide is in great difficulty and not easily restored due to the various unresolved problems between countries. I firmly believe that international problems can only be resolved through sincere cooperation to achieve satisfactory goals for the happiness of the world and the interests of our country. China must do its utmost to support all countries at this conference to achieve the complete objectives of this meeting. As for the other main points, I have already discussed them fully at the farewell banquet for the public associations yesterday, so I will not repeat them. This trip will last about two months. I am grateful to you, my friends and relatives, for sending me off. I cannot thank you all individually. I hope you will guide me at any time and inform me of domestic news from time to time. I will also report the progress of the meeting to you.

Taxpayer Association Sends Three Important Letters to the Municipal Council 100

Opposing the Management, Inspection, or Supervision of Factories

Hiring a Qualified Chinese Auditor to Audit Accounts

The Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers' Association, yesterday, based on the resolutions of the Association's Delegates' Meeting on April 12 and the reply from the Shanghai Real Estate Association, sent three important letters to the Shanghai Municipal Council, which are recorded below:

Factory Management Rights

To the Director: It is found that at the Delegates' Meeting of this Association on April 12, regarding your Council's plan to manage factories within the concession, it was resolved that, "According to the opinion of this Delegates' Meeting, most of the work in the factories in the Public Concession is done by Chinese workers. If factory management regulations are established in addition to the labor laws and regulations promulgated by the Chinese government, it will harm Chinese sovereignty. Therefore, it is resolved that any proposal or land regulations and or amendments to the attached laws that grant the Municipal Council the right to manage, inspect, or supervise all factories within the concession are considered an act of exceeding authority and will not be agreed to." I am sending this letter to your Council for your information and action.

Chinese Auditor

To the Director: It is found that at the Delegates' Meeting of this Association on April 12, regarding the addition of a Chinese auditor to your Council, it was resolved that, "According to the opinion of this Delegates' Meeting, in order to satisfy the wishes of our Chinese citizens and adapt to the needs of the environment, it is necessary for the Shanghai Municipal Council to hire a qualified Chinese person to audit accounts. This Association hereby authorizes the Municipal Council to proceed with all necessary procedures so that the appointment of a Chinese auditor can be realized as soon as possible." I am sending this letter to your Council for your information and action.　　Chinese Committee Member for Land

To the Director: It is found that one of the two Chinese members of your Council's Land Committee for the years 1933-1934 has already been appointed by this Association's Delegates' Meeting, Dr. Chen Tingrui, and a letter has been sent to your Council. The other member should be appointed by the Chinese landowners' association. This Association informed the Shanghai Real Estate Association on April 7 to elect. Later, we received a reply from the association, nominating Mr. Feng Bingnan as the member of the association elected by the Chinese landowners. I am sending this letter for your information and action.

Public Performance Yesterday 102

Morning Performance at the Bund Caused Traffic Congestion

Japanese Also Went to See the Afternoon Performance at Longhua

The Shanghai China Aviation Company's newly imported Best Eagle brand fighter plane, sold by US Transportation in Shanghai, has been test flying at Longhua for several days. The pilot is the famous American aviator Mr. Du Lide, who has won a flying medal in the United States. He performed separately yesterday morning and afternoon. Although it was drizzling in the afternoon, no fewer than a thousand Chinese and Western spectators went to Longhua. The details are recorded below.

Aircraft Structure: The fighter plane is a biplane single-seater with a fuselage length of approximately 40 meters. The fuselage is brown, and the wings are painted yellow. The aircraft is manufactured by the American Curtiss factory and is equipped with a 700-horsepower engine. It can be equipped with a machine gun for combat.

Bund Performance: At 11:00 a.m. yesterday, the sound of the engine was heard in the sky over the city. Shortly after, Mr. Du's plane flew around the Bund and the Huangpu River for a week, and then began the performance, such as flying straight up and sideways. There were many forms, and even several times, the aircraft flew with its belly facing the sky, which was truly not easy. This caused the general public to stop and watch. There were especially many spectators on the Bund, and the road was almost blocked. Everyone was full of praise. After half an hour, he flew back to Longhua and landed.

Longhua Test Flight: At 4:30 p.m., Mr. Du continued the test flight at the Longhua Airport. Since the people of Shanghai had not seen the full picture of the morning performance, even though it was drizzling and the road was muddy, those who went to Longhua in the afternoon were still very crowded. Students from a certain girls' school also took field trucks to the scene, which was especially noteworthy. Three Japanese men, all dressed in civilian clothes, watched the show in the field and silently observed the planes. The car they were riding in belonged to the headquarters of the Marine Corps. It is thought that they were Japanese soldiers, who admired Mr. Du's flying, so they went to watch in civilian clothes. There were more than a hundred Chinese and Western cars in the field, and the number of people was about a thousand. At four o'clock, the plane was originally parked in front of the China Aviation Company's factory warehouse. Another engineer opened and tested the motor. After testing for half an hour, Mr. Du put on a white aviation suit, put on a parachute, and boarded the plane. He was towed out of the airfield by car, and then he soared into the sky, performing various techniques. Finally, the pilot stretched his hands out of the plane. The film company and photographers went to take pictures and then dispersed. It is said that the plane is the latest American yellow biplane single-seater fighter, with 700 horsepower. The plane can be equipped with a machine gun, but it was not installed because it is now a performance test flight.

The Yangtze River Train Ferry Has Arrived in Shanghai 103

Postponed for Three Months Before Sailing to Beijing

The Yangtze River train ferry, which was ordered by the Ministry of Transportation from the United Kingdom and is used to connect the Tianjin-Pukou and Shanghai-Nanjing lines, sailed into the Huangpu River a few days ago and dropped anchor outside the Zhoujiazuijiao at the 39th and 40th buoys. These buoys are flying red flags. It has been a little over two months since it set sail on February 15. The ship is 372 feet long, 54 and a half feet at its widest, and can carry 1,480 tons. There are three sets of tracks on the deck, each 300 feet long, which can accommodate three trains, each of which can pull seven cars. The car heads for the deck that are used to carry the cars are also manufactured in the United Kingdom and will be shipped soon. When the Yangtze River set sail from England, it had not yet been completed. The ship's speed can reach 12 and a half nautical miles per hour. Currently, because the bridge on both sides of Nanjing Pukou is not yet completed, it is said that it will be postponed for three months before it can sail to Beijing for use.

General Trade Union Cables Request to Stop Cotton Mills from Reducing Working Hours 104

Cable to the Ministry of Industry

The Shanghai General Trade Union cabled the National Government's Ministry of Industry yesterday, stating, "It is submitted that the Chinese Cotton Mill Association has illegally resolved to reduce working hours. We implore you to issue a clear order to stop it to protect the industry and maintain the livelihood of the workers. Our country's industry has always been dominated by silk and tea, which has a long history. Unfortunately, the holders of these industries are all greedy for short-term gains and produce crude and shoddy products, resulting in successive bankruptcies. The only surviving industry in our country is the cotton industry. If the authorities of the industry do not want to follow in the footsteps of silk and tea, how should they strive to make progress? However, it was reported on April 11 that the Chinese Cotton Mill Association, citing the dumping of foreign goods and overproduction, resolved that, starting from April 22, all Chinese cotton mills nationwide would uniformly reduce working hours by one day per week. If the resolution is violated, it will be punished according to regulations. We investigate that in recent years, due to the increasing foreign aggression and economic decline, all industries in our country have shown a downturn. The industry, which is the leader of all industries in our country, should make every effort to revitalize itself to compete with foreign goods, thereby saving the precarious industry. However, they have ignored the overall situation and acted in a way that is counterproductive, suddenly using the negative method of reducing working hours, so that foreign goods can have a greater opportunity to dump. Because after the Chinese factories reduce working hours, foreign goods will inevitably increase production and rush to manufacture. This reduction of working hours will not only affect the livelihoods of hundreds of thousands of workers, but also be of utmost importance to the future of the industry. At this time of serious national crisis, labor and capital should sincerely join hands to save the country from danger. Moreover, the profit or loss of business depends on whether the management is appropriate. At present, factories such as Shenxin No. 1 Factory and Minsheng Factory all feel that production is insufficient. Based on this speculation, it is not necessarily the case that there are no factories in the country that are in the same situation as Shenxin. However, the association used the word "through" to force all cotton mills in the country to reduce working hours uniformly, which is extremely illegal. Moreover, the resolution has not been approved by the government, not only is it legally baseless, but it also despises the law. As an association, for the sake of the workers' lives and for the sake of Chinese industry, we are determined to oppose this illegal reduction of working hours. For this reason, we urgently submit this petition, imploring your ministry to issue a clear order to stop it in order to maintain the industry and resolve disputes, which would be of great benefit. Respectfully submitted to the Ministry of Industry.

Taxpaying Westerners Held Annual Meeting and Special Meeting Today 113

Discussing Amendments to the Land Regulations

Chinese Do Not Agree to Infringement on Our Sovereignty

Taxpaying Westerners in the Public Concession will hold their annual meeting at the Paramount Theatre on Nanjing West Road at 4 p.m. today. At 5 p.m., they will continue to hold a special meeting to amend the land regulations in an attempt to seize the right to manage factories. Citizens of the city, the Chinese Ratepayers Association, and the municipal government are all arguing on the basis of reason. The details are as follows:

Meeting Today

The annual meeting of taxpaying Westerners has a total of eight proposals, including one new proposal: the Shanghai Municipal Council purchasing land to build a city hall and library. The special meeting of taxpaying Westerners has a proposal to amend the first line of Article 34 of the land regulations by adding the words "owning or occupying or opening factories or workshops or engaging in industry" after the words "within the concession" in an attempt to seize the right to manage factories. The Shanghai Municipal Council estimates that a total of more than 3,780 votes are eligible to attend the annual meeting of taxpaying Westerners. The quorum for the meeting is more than one-third, or 1,262 votes.

Our Attitude

According to the Shanghai Municipal Council, it is expected that the amendment to Article 30 of the land regulations of the Public Concession will be passed at today's special meeting. It is rumored that the municipal government, for this issue, had Yu Hongjun, the secretary-general, make representations to the director-general of the Shanghai Municipal Council in advance. However, when a reporter from the New Life News Agency interviewed Yu yesterday and asked about this matter, Yu denied that he had negotiated with Fei, and said that our side would wait until it was passed before discussing countermeasures. There is nothing to announce at this time.

Shanghai Municipal Council Attempts to Seize the Right to Manage Factories Xie Fusheng Expresses His Opinion 114

Regarding the Shanghai Municipal Council's new proposal to the special meeting of taxpaying Westerners that all factories in the concession must obtain licenses, Xie Fusheng sent a letter to the Western newspapers in English yesterday, holding a very insightful and appropriate view. The New Life News Agency has obtained the original and translated the gist as follows: "At the special meeting of taxpaying Westerners in the Public Concession on the 19th of this month (it is said that this special meeting requires 1,200 votes to reach the quorum), the Shanghai Municipal Council will propose to amend Article 34 of the Yangjingbang Regulations, intending to obtain unprecedented and unlimited powers at once through a very simple licensing method. All factory owners, factory buildings, work, and any industrial operations are under the Shanghai Municipal Council's flexible management. The taxpayers in the concession, regardless of Chinese or Western nationality, are focused on commercial interests, and they generally do not pay attention to the Yangjingbang Regulations that created this Public Concession and the Shanghai Municipal Council. If one were to analyze the wording of Article 34 of the Regulations, one would know that Article 34 has nothing to do with factory management. The article stipulates that "within the concession, all

markets, vegetable markets, clubs, boarding houses, music venues, theaters, circuses, cinemas, restaurants, entertainment venues, hotels, saunas, billiard rooms, skating rinks, dance halls, brothels:: milk sheds, laundries, bakeries, slaughterhouses, carriage lines, car lines, cattle sheds, sheep sheds, pig sheds must be licensed by the Shanghai Municipal Council before they can be opened. Also, all second-hand clothing stores, hotels, sales of various harmful drugs, poisons, and manufactured medicines, butcher shops, fruit stores, ice stores, vegetable stores, tobacco shops, and lottery shops must be licensed. Also, all small boats, equipped for personal use or for public transport, sampans, small steamers, ferries, horses, donkeys, mules, cars, motorized bicycles, rickshaws, hand-carried litters, carts, trams who own or operate these are liable to licensing. Anyone who keeps a dog is certainly among those required to be licensed. Under the regulations, the Shanghai Municipal Council has the right to formulate rules separately according to the circumstances for the handling of licenses, take security, and fine violators up to 100 yuan. Those who continue to violate the rules will be fined 25 yuan every 24 hours. What we can clearly see is that the rules on the license must be fully complied with by the licensee, and the Shanghai Municipal Council has the freedom to formulate these rules. I know that the Shanghai Municipal Council's proposal will be justified by the fact that factories in the concession have suffered fires and the tragic deaths of workers, and will criticize the Chinese Factory Law as being too idealistic and unsuitable for the actual economic conditions of Chinese workers. However, the problem facing us today is not whether the factory conditions need to be relieved and improved to protect the health and safety of workers, and if only this is discussed, no one will object. However, what we should focus on is whether the Shanghai Municipal Council's attempt to obtain powers beyond the scope of municipal affairs by means of amending the regulations is simply a futile effort. If the Shanghai Municipal Council only needs to amend a completely irrelevant regulation to achieve its goal of managing factories, then the Shanghai Municipal Council is a hundred times smarter than Feitang. Feitang has spent several months studying the present and future problems of the Public Concession, and has also made some statements on China's Factory Law. Chapter 8 of his report says that "in all fairness, all the provisions of the Chinese Factory Law are too close to the ideal. The Factory Law may need to be amended in order to proceed gradually, but in any case, the concession authorities must not act independently in formulating any regulations on industry. For the sake of the concession authorities, the best way is to take the Chinese Factory Law as the standard, and formulate regulations within the scope of possibility, in order to make the regulations that factories in the concession and factories in the Chinese territory should comply with not too different." Furthermore, even if the special meeting on the 19th reaches a quorum and the new proposal is passed by the whole, the Shanghai Municipal Council's smooth sailing proposal may only be a self-consolation. Article 11 of the Yangjingbang Regulations says, "The board of directors has the right to formulate other regulations at any time in order to improve the various articles of the regulations." It also says, "The rules formulated by the board of directors must be approved by the ministers of the various countries stationed in Beijing, or a majority of them, and a special meeting of the tenant rate payers (i.e. the special meeting of the taxpayers) must be held to agree before they can be implemented." In short, the Shanghai Municipal Council's desire to obtain the right to manage factories can never arise under Article 34 or any regulations. The only way for the Shanghai Municipal Council is to amend the Yangjingbang Regulations, because in terms of what is clearly stipulated in the regulations, licensing and factory management are both illegal. Moreover, Article 27 of the Amendments to the Yangjingbang Regulations stipulates even more clearly that Feitang once told us, "Whenever there is a matter of amending the land regulations, it must still be handled through negotiations between China and the various countries. The Shanghai Municipal Council only needs to submit the suggestions for amendment."

Hebei Association Welcomes Song Zheyuan's Representatives 116

The Hebei Association in Shanghai held a registration committee meeting yesterday afternoon. A total of 191 committee members attended, with Sun Hongyi presiding and Yu Jisu recording. Song Zheyuan's representatives, Xiao Xiange and Sun Longji, also braved the rain to attend. The meeting began at 2 p.m. with formalities. The chairman first introduced Xiao and Sun to the audience, expressed welcome, and expressed gratitude to Song's army for their hard fighting and sacrifice in protecting North China. Then, Xiao was invited to speak about the bitter fighting in Xifengkou for a month. The scene was tragic and the whole atmosphere was somber, with some even weeping. The most heroic acts were the killing of the enemy outside Xifengkou and the seven entries and exits in the battle for Haiyangzhen. The tragedy was that the broadsword team fought against artillery fire, with flesh and blood flying everywhere. However, due to the lack of supplies and inadequate equipment, the wounded died tragically. The biggest shortcomings were the lack of unified command and waiting for the enemy to attack, allowing the enemy to take advantage of the situation and break through with one blow. It is hoped that all sectors of the public will provide spiritual encouragement and material assistance to the front line, and urge the government to strictly order all armies to attack together. Otherwise, the fall of Pingjin is imminent, Hebei will be lost, and the entire North China will not be protected, and we will all become slaves of a conquered nation. The chairman then painfully explained the advantages and disadvantages of the Hebei Association in Shanghai seeking unity. Registration is unity, and saving the homeland and saving the country depends entirely on this action. We must register and unite our fellow villagers, actively provide material assistance to the front line, and unite with various groups to telegraph the government to seek a unified strategy to deal with foreign aggression. This is a spiritual call. Then, the method of registration was discussed. Yang Jitian, Zhang Ziyong, and Mou Ziming all spoke successively. As a result of the discussion, registration and solicitation will be carried out separately. After contacting the fundraising agencies to assist the anti-Japanese armies, they will immediately proceed, donating and remitting funds as they go. Due to the rain, no photos could be taken. The meeting ended at 6 p.m.

Wang Xiaoying Talks About the Military Situation and Popular Sentiment in North China 117

Shen Huilian, Wang Xiaoying, and Wei Qiongying, representatives of the China Women's Relief Association for Compatriots in the Northeast Comfort Delegation, carried 42 boxes of comfort goods to the front line in the Northeast to comfort the troops. They returned to Shanghai a few days ago and will hold a general meeting at 2 p.m. today to report on the process and discuss plans to donate more funds or purchase more comfort goods. A reporter from the Central News Agency visited Ms. Wang Xiaoying at Wuben Women's School yesterday to inquire about the situation in the north. The following is a summary:

Military Situation: Fervor

Ms. Wang said that when the representatives left the front line, the war was calm, as if in a truce. Only when they boarded the train in Tianjin to return south did they learn from the newspapers that the war had started again and that the various passes of the Great Wall were in danger. The situation must have changed. The representatives brought a total of 42 boxes of comfort goods, including towels, cigarettes, dry food, and goggles. After arriving in Peiping, they contacted the military authorities and went to the front line of each pass to comfort the troops. The soldiers everywhere were very motivated, especially the lower-ranking officers, who were like madmen all day long. Their sincere patriotism was inspiring. The situation at Xifengkou was better than at other passes, and the morale of the defending soldiers was even higher. However, the lack of weapons and equipment and the hasty construction of defensive works were truly disheartening. Moreover, because the terrain inside the pass was flat, the occupied positions were also less favorable. It was difficult to win against an enemy army with sophisticated weapons and a large number of soldiers. However, the soldiers' eagerness to kill the enemy was commendable. Therefore, even if we lose troops and cede territory, the people of the country must continue to provide material assistance. At present, there is sufficient food on the front line. What is lacking is guns, ammunition, and transportation. The Women's Association will hold a general meeting tomorrow (i.e. today) to report on the process and plan to donate funds.

Popular Sentiment: Depression

The reporter then inquired about the popular sentiment and social situation in Peiping and Tianjin. According to Ms. Wang, the Peiping and Tianjin areas were safe, and the city was the same as before. The business in Peiping and Tianjin may even be more prosperous than before. The peace and tranquility of the popular sentiment was beyond expectation. The two places were less than a few hundred miles away from the passes of the Great Wall. Outside this distance of a few hours, the national war was so fierce, and the people there could still live and work in peace, without panic or tension. This situation was truly surprising. However, since Yu Xuezhong took office in Tianjin, the Japanese army's malicious provocations have gradually subsided. The Japanese concession is open all night and the area is also quiet.

Investigation of the Business Boundaries of the General and Branch Offices of the Ministry of Communications Telephone Bureau 122

Manual Switching Still Used Outside the Southern City and Zhabei

After the Shanghai Telephone Bureau implements automatic telephone service, it will implement a moderate increase in telephone charges starting on May 1, as reported in yesterday's newspaper. The following is a list of the telephone service boundaries of the general and branch offices, and the method of communication between Longhua and other areas and Zhabei and the Southern City:

Boundaries of Each Bureau 1. Southern City General Bureau: North to the French Concession, East to the Huangpu River, South to the Huangpu River, West to the Rihui Port. 2. Longhua Branch Bureau: North to the French Concession and Xujiahui River, East to the Rihui Port, West to the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway, South to the Longhua Port and the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway. 3. Zhabei Branch Bureau: North to Tanzhawan, East to the Shajing Port, South to the Public Concession and the Suzhou River, West to Bridge No. 2 of the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway. 4. Jiangwan Branch Bureau: Limited to the Jiangwan Town street and the city center area. 5. Nanxiang Branch Bureau: Limited to the Nanxiang town street. 6. Pudong Branch Bureau: (To be determined after establishment). 7. Wusong Branch Bureau: Limited to the Wusong town street. 8. Zhenru Branch Bureau: Limited to the Zhenru town street and the Jilin University area.

Method of Communication 1. When users in the Southern City and Zhabei districts want to communicate with users in any of the Longhua (including Fahua), Jiangwan, Zhenru, Nanxiang, Wusong, etc. districts, they should first dial the number of the branch office or branch of that district. After an operator answers, they should inform the operator of the other party's number and they will be able to communicate at any time. 2. When users in the Longhua, Jiangwan, Zhenru, Nanxiang, Wusong, etc. districts want to communicate with users in any of the Southern City and Zhabei districts, they can follow the telephone usage method for people and inform the operator of the user's number and they will be able to communicate at any time.

Labor Unrest at Nanyang Tobacco Company Becomes Serious Again 123

Company Suddenly Fires Fifteen Workers

Trade Union Petitions Party and Government for Speedy Mediation

The labor unrest at the Nanyang Tobacco Company on East Broadway Road, after the mediation by party and government agencies and the Municipal Federation of Trade Unions, had temporarily ended, and the situation had been eased. However, the company suddenly posted an announcement a few days ago (the 17th) announcing the dismissal of Wu Shiyuan, Zhang Zhang, Li Gui, Li Xinfa, and 11 other former trade union officials, causing the labor unrest to become serious again. The Nanyang Office immediately reported to the Fourth District Cigarette Trade Union to request negotiations. The union, upon receiving the report, was deeply concerned about the expansion of the unrest. Therefore, in addition to notifying the workers to work with peace of mind and wait for a resolution, it specifically submitted a petition to the party and government agencies yesterday, requesting speedy mediation.

Shanghai-Ningbo Hongxing Steamer Changes Route 124

Zhuang Songfu and Others Request No Change of Route

Since the January 28 Incident last year, the Shanghai-Ningbo route has been extremely crowded due to the dangerous environment. At that time, fortunately, the Daxing Shipping Company, in view of the suffering of the refugees from Ningbo and Shaoxing, who were exposed to wind and rain, sent the Hongxing steamer to add voyages on a daily basis, which benefited merchants and travelers. This was no small feat. After the incident, the steamer continued to seek reforms, reducing liquor fees, and relieving the burden on the general poor merchants and travelers, and was praised by the people of Ningbo and Shaoxing. It is now reported that Mr. Xu of the Hongxing Shipping Company has accepted the movement of other Shanghai-Ningbo shipping companies and intends to change the route of the steamer. People from Shanghai and Ningbo heard the news and felt indignant. The village elder, Mr. Zhuang Songfu, and others, considering that if the steamer stops sailing, it will have a significant impact on the poor merchants and travelers in Ningbo and Shaoxing, sent a letter to Mr. Xu, urging him to uphold his long-cherished aspiration to care for his fellow villagers, adhere to his original intention, and never be restrained by money or oppressed by force, and fight to the end to benefit the hundreds of thousands of poor fellow villagers in Shanghai. It is not yet known how Mr. Xu will respond after receiving the letter.
